If there are many streams\n715:   // that may result in a stack overflow. This flag is used to avoid above recursion.\n716:   if (drained_due_to_premature_resets_) {\n717:     return;\n718:   }\n719: \n720:   if (closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ == 0) {\n721:     return;\n722:   }\n723: \n724:   const uint64_t limit =\n725:       runtime_.snapshot().getInteger(ConnectionManagerImpl::PrematureResetTotalStreamCountKey, 500);\n726: \n727:   if (closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ < limit) {\n728:     // Even though the total number of streams have not reached `limit`, check if the number of bad\n729:     // streams is high enough that even if every subsequent stream is good, the connection\n730:     // would be closed once the limit is reached, and if so close the connection now.\n731:     if (number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < limit) {\n732:       return;\n733:     }\n734:   } else {\n735:     if (number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_) {\n736:       return;\n737:     }\n738:   }\n739: \n740:   if (read_callbacks_->connection().state() == Network::Connection::State::Open) {\n741:     stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_.inc();\n742: \n743:     // Mark the the connection has been drained due to too many premature resets.\n744:     drained_due_to_premature_resets_ = true;\n745: \n746:     doConnectionClose(Network::ConnectionCloseType::Abort, absl::nullopt,\n747:                       \"too_many_premature_resets\");\n748:   }\n749: }\n750: \n751: void ConnectionManagerImpl::onGoAway(GoAwayErrorCode) {\n752:   // Currently we do nothing with remote go away frames. void ConnectionManagerImpl::ActiveStream::maybeRecordLastByteReceived(bool end_stream) {\n1303:   // If recreateStream is called, the HCM rewinds state and may send more encodeData calls.\n1304:   if complicated, but important.\n1312: //\n1313: // We want to do minimal work before selecting route and creating a filter\n1314: // chain to maximize the number of requests which get custom filter behavior,\n1315: // e.g. registering access logging.\n1316: //\n1317: // This must be balanced by doing sanity checking for invalid requests (one\n1318: // can't route select properly without full headers), checking state required to\n1319: // serve error responses (connection close, head requests, etc), and\n1320: // modifications which may themselves affect route selection.\n1321: void {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01Mid6Vhuxq6qTv1DQ8p63WS","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01Kh2mzSQFDcujuuWj1QNRvU","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/coverage_analysis.md","content":"# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager\n\n## Summary\n\nThis analysis identifies 8 critical test coverage gaps in Envoy's HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) implementation that could allow subtle bugs to slip through. The gaps primarily involve error handling paths, edge cases in connection state management, and complex interactions between filter chains and stream lifecycle management. The most critical gaps involve premature reset detection, HTTP/1 safe drain logic, and zombie stream cleanup coordination.\n\n---\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: Premature Stream Reset Detection with Runtime Threshold Logic\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~702-749 (method `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()`)\n**Risk**: **HIGH**\n\n**Description**:\n\nThe `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` method contains complex threshold logic that triggers connection draining when streams are reset prematurely. The function:\n\n1. Checks a runtime configuration key `PrematureResetTotalStreamCountKey` (default 500)\n2. Implements a counter-based heuristic: `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < limit`\n3. Has recursion prevention via `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` flag\n4. Increments stats only under specific conditions\n5. Performs early return with different conditions depending on whether `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_` exceeds the limit\n\nCurrently, no tests exercise the full decision tree with various combinations of:\n- Stream reset counts just below/above the threshold\n- Runtime parameter override scenarios\n- Recursion prevention correctness\n- Edge case where exactly `limit/2` streams are reset\n\n**Proposed Test**: `PrematureStreamResetTriggersConnectionDrainAtThreshold`\n- **Setup**: Create 251 requests, 251 with premature resets, runtime limit set to 500\n- **Action**: Trigger drain check\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Verify `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` stat is incremented\n  - Verify connection receives `doConnectionClose()` call\n  - Verify flag prevents recursive drain calls\n  - Verify `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` prevents re-entrance\n\n**Why It Matters**: Premature reset detection is a security/abuse-prevention mechanism. Incorrect threshold calculations could allow attackers to exhaust resources or prevent legitimate connection draining. The complex inequality checks are error-prone.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: HTTP/1 Safe Max Connection Duration with Soft Drain\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~769-787 (method `onConnectionDurationTimeout()`, specifically HTTP1 soft drain path)\n**Risk**: **HIGH**\n\n**Description**:\n\nWhen `config_->http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration()` is true and the codec protocol is HTTP/1, the connection manager takes a \"soft drain\" path instead of a graceful drain sequence:\n\n```cpp\nif (config_->http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration() && codec_->protocol() < Protocol::Http2) {\n  stats_.named_.downstream_cx_http1_soft_drain_.inc();\n  soft_drain_http1_ = true;\n} else {\n  startDrainSequence();\n}\n```\n\nThis sets `soft_drain_http1_` flag but doesn't immediately trigger drain. The flag must be checked elsewhere to actually prevent new requests. No tests verify:\n- That soft drain prevents new requests from being accepted\n- That existing requests are allowed to complete\n- That the stat is correctly incremented\n- Interaction between soft drain and max connection duration\n- What happens when non-HTTP1 protocol reaches max duration (should do full drain sequence)\n\n**Proposed Test**: `HTTP1SafeMaxConnectionDurationSoftDrain`\n- **Setup**: Create HTTP/1.1 connection with `http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration=true`, set connection max duration\n- **Action**: Wait for max duration timeout\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Verify `downstream_cx_http1_soft_drain_` is incremented (not `downstream_cx_max_duration_reached_`)\n  - Verify `soft_drain_http1_` flag is set\n  - Create new request and verify it completes without delay\n  - Verify connection doesn't close until all streams finish\n  - Verify stat names distinguish this from other drain types\n\n**Why It Matters**: HTTP/1 safe drain is a special case designed to prevent race conditions. Testing this specific code path is essential because it diverges from normal drain logic and could leave connections in inconsistent states.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: Zombie Stream Cleanup with Watermark Coordination\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~2137-2179 (methods `onCodecEncodeComplete()` and `onCodecLowLevelReset()`)\n**Risk**: **HIGH**\n\n**Description**:\n\nWhen a stream reaches end-of-stream via `doEndStream()`, it becomes a \"zombie stream\" marked by `state_.is_zombie_stream_ = true`. The zombie stream persists until the codec completes encoding. This coordination involves:\n\n1. Checking `state_.codec_encode_complete_` flag\n2. Calling `shouldSkipDeferredCloseDelay()` to determine if close can be immediate\n3. Possibly triggering `connection_manager_.close_connection_on_zombie_stream_complete_`\n4. Calling `checkForDeferredClose()` after stream destruction\n\nThe gap: No tests verify the complete lifecycle of zombie streams under conditions:\n- With deferred close delay vs. immediate close\n- When multiple zombie streams exist in parallel\n- When connection close is triggered while zombies still exist\n- When watermark callbacks fire on a zombie stream\n- Interaction with `connection_manager_.close_connection_on_zombie_stream_complete_` flag\n\n**Proposed Test**: `ZombieStreamCleanupWithConnectionCloseFlag`\n- **Setup**: Create 3 concurrent streams, enable `close_connection_on_zombie_stream_complete_` flag\n- **Action**: Send response with end_stream on all streams nearly simultaneously\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Verify first stream becomes zombie\n  - Verify second and third streams also become zombies\n  - Verify no `doDeferredStreamDestroy()` until codec encode complete\n  - Verify `checkForDeferredClose()` called with correct `skip_delay` value\n  - Verify connection closes after last zombie cleanup\n  - Verify high watermark events don't crash or corrupt state during cleanup\n\n**Why It Matters**: Zombie streams represent a complex state transition that could cause memory leaks, connection hangs, or protocol violations if not handled correctly. The interaction with the deferred close logic is particularly subtle.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: Connection Upgrade Rejection with Smuggling Prevention\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1546-1563 (method `decodeHeaders()`, upgrade rejection path)\n**Risk**: **MEDIUM**\n\n**Description**:\n\nAfter detecting an upgrade request is rejected by the route, the code enforces a strict policy:\n\n```cpp\nif (create_chain_result.upgradeRejected()) {\n  // Close connection to prevent HTTP smuggling via upgrade payload\n  sendLocalReply(Code::UpgradeRequired, /* ... */);\n  connection_manager_.doConnectionClose(...);\n  return;\n}\n```\n\nThe logic prevents HTTP request smuggling when an Upgrade header is present but the route rejects the upgrade. However, tests don't verify:\n- That connection closes when `upgradeRejected()` is true\n- Various upgrade header combinations (CONNECT, Upgrade: websocket, etc.)\n- That the error response is sent before connection close\n- Behavior when upgrade is rejected for different routes\n- Interaction with other connection close conditions\n\n**Proposed Test**: `UpgradeRejectedByRouteClosesConnection`\n- **Setup**: Configure route that rejects WebSocket upgrades\n- **Action**: Send HTTP/1.1 GET request with Upgrade: websocket and Connection: upgrade headers\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Verify `create_chain_result.upgradeRejected()` is true\n  - Verify `sendLocalReply()` called with `Code::UpgradeRequired`\n  - Verify `doConnectionClose()` called\n  - Verify no further data is processed after upgrade rejection\n  - Try sending pipelined request after upgrade rejection - verify it's rejected\n\n**Why It Matters**: HTTP request smuggling is a critical security vulnerability. This code path protects against a specific smuggling vector, so it must be thoroughly tested to prevent regression.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: Request Header Validation Error Paths\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1415-1432 (method `decodeHeaders()`, header validation section)\n**Risk**: **MEDIUM**\n\n**Description**:\n\nThe `decodeHeaders()` method performs multiple sanity checks on request headers:\n\n1. Line 1415-1420: Verify Host header exists\n2. Line 1423-1431: Validate headers via `HeaderUtility::requestHeadersValid()`\n3. Line 1427-1429: Handle codec error notification conditionally based on `streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage()`\n\nTest gaps:\n- Missing test for requests without Host header (particularly HTTP/1.1 which requires it)\n- No test for invalid header combinations caught by `HeaderUtility::requestHeadersValid()`\n- The conditional codec error path (line 1427) is not tested: when `streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage()` is false, `handleCodecError()` is called, but when it's true, it's skipped\n- No test verifies that `sendLocalReply()` with `Code::BadRequest` is actually sent\n- No tests for header combinations that pass Host check but fail validity check\n\n**Proposed Test**: `InvalidRequestHeadersTriggersLocalReply`\n- **Setup**: Two variants - one with missing Host header, one with invalid header combination\n- **Action**: Send request with missing/invalid headers\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Verify `sendLocalReply(Code::BadRequest, ...)` called\n  - Verify response code details match (MissingHost vs other)\n  - For variant 2: Verify `handleCodecError()` called when `streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage()` is false\n  - Verify stats incremented\n  - Verify stream is terminated after local reply\n\n**Why It Matters**: Header validation is a first-line defense against malformed requests. Incomplete testing could allow invalid requests to progress through the filter chain.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 6: Path Normalization with Redirect and Rejection\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1460-1487 (method `decodeHeaders()`, path normalization section)\n**Risk**: **MEDIUM**\n\n**Description**:\n\nPath normalization has three possible outcomes with different code paths:\n\n1. `NormalizePathAction::Reject` (line 1467) - close connection\n2. `NormalizePathAction::Redirect` (line 1474) - send 307 with Location header\n3. `NormalizePathAction::Continue` (line 1486) - allow request to continue\n4. Special case: gRPC requests with Redirect (line 1468-1469) - reject instead\n\nTest gaps:\n- No test for path normalization returning `Reject` and verifying connection close\n- Limited tests for `Redirect` case with Location header construction\n- No test for the gRPC special case (reject redirect instead of allowing it)\n- No test with UHV disabled (the normalization code is skipped in UHV mode)\n- Stats tracking for `downstream_rq_failed_path_normalization_` and `downstream_rq_redirected_with_normalized_path_` may not be fully tested\n\n**Proposed Test**: `PathNormalizationRejectClosesConnection`\n- **Setup**: Route with path normalization enabled, request with path requiring rejection\n- **Action**: Send request with path like `//foo` or other normalization-requiring path\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Verify path normalization action is `Reject`\n  - Verify `sendLocalReply(Code::BadRequest)` called\n  - Verify `downstream_rq_failed_path_normalization_` stat incremented\n  - Verify connection close is triggered\n  - Verify gRPC request with redirect returns `BadRequest` not `TemporaryRedirect`\n\n**Why It Matters**: Path normalization is security-critical. Path traversal and normalization bypasses are well-known attack vectors.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 7: Metadata Processing with Filter Chain Iteration\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc`\n**Lines**: ~880-920 (method `decodeMetadata()`) and `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` lines ~1650-1656\n**Risk**: **MEDIUM**\n\n**Description**:\n\nMetadata is processed through the decoder filter chain with special handling for newly-added metadata:\n\n1. Initial metadata is passed through filters via `filter_manager_.decodeMetadata()`\n2. During header decoding, filters can add new metadata via `addDecodedMetadata()`\n3. `processNewlyAddedMetadata()` must be called to iterate newly-added metadata through the chain\n4. Metadata can cause stream errors if there are issues\n\nTest gaps:\n- No test for metadata being added by one filter and properly reaching all subsequent filters\n- No test for the case where metadata processing fails or a filter returns error status\n- No test for concurrent metadata and data events (metadata while data is buffered)\n- No test for metadata with deferred stream (when decode is deferred to next I/O cycle)\n- The deferred metadata path (line 1654) has minimal test coverage\n\n**Proposed Test**: `MetadataProcessingWithFilterChainIteration`\n- **Setup**: Create 2 decoder filters, first filter adds metadata in `decodeHeaders()`\n- **Action**: Send request headers, verify metadata flows through filter chain\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Verify first filter receives original metadata (if any)\n  - Verify second filter receives newly-added metadata from first filter\n  - Verify `processNewlyAddedMetadata()` is called\n  - Verify both filters' `decodeMetadata()` called with correct metadata\n  - Test error case: if `decodeMetadata()` on second filter fails, verify stream is reset\n  - Test deferred case: metadata added when stream decode is deferred\n\n**Why It Matters**: Metadata processing affects request routing, rate limiting, and other policy decisions. Bugs here could cause incorrect policy application or filter chain violations.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 8: Concurrent Stream Watermark Coordination with Connection Close\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~2113-2121 (methods `onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()` and `onBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark()`)\n**Risk**: **MEDIUM**\n\n**Description**:\n\nWhen connection buffers cross watermarks, callbacks are propagated to all active streams:\n\n```cpp\nvoid onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark() {\n  codec_->onUnderlyingConnectionAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark();\n}\n```\n\nThis calls the codec which propagates to individual streams. Test gaps:\n- No test for watermark callback when connection is draining\n- No test for watermark callback when some streams are zombies\n- No test for what happens if a filter throws exception in watermark callback\n- No test for rapid watermark threshold crossing (above/below/above/below)\n- No test for watermark callback interacting with stream idle timeout\n- Interaction with filter callbacks like `callHighWatermarkCallbacks()`\n\n**Proposed Test**: `WatermarkCallbackDuringConnectionDrain`\n- **Setup**: Create 2 concurrent streams, set write buffer low watermark\n- **Action**:\n  1. Fill write buffer to trigger high watermark\n  2. Start drain sequence\n  3. Continue receiving data to trigger more writes\n  4. Drain write buffer to trigger low watermark\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Verify high watermark callbacks don't crash during drain\n  - Verify low watermark callbacks don't crash during drain\n  - Verify stream codec callbacks coordinated with connection callbacks\n  - Verify filters' high/low watermark callbacks called for each stream\n  - Verify no deadlock with concurrent watermark events\n\n**Why It Matters**: Watermark handling under drain conditions is subtle. Backpressure coordination bugs could cause buffer overflows, deadlocks, or connection leaks.\n\n---\n\n## File References\n\n### Key Implementation Files Analyzed:\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` (2500+ lines, complex state machine)\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h` (header definitions and interfaces)\n- `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` (filter chain execution)\n- `source/common/http/filter_manager.h` (filter manager state)\n\n### Test Files Analyzed:\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc` (main tests)\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_2.cc` (response ordering tests)\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_3.cc` (filter body injection tests)\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_base.h` (test base class with mocks)\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_misc_test.cc` (miscellaneous tests)\n\n### Supporting Test Infrastructure:\n- `test/mocks/http/mocks.h` (mock codec, encoder, decoder)\n- `test/mocks/router/mocks.h` (mock route config)\n\n---\n\n## Recommendations for Test Implementation\n\n1. **Use existing test infrastructure**: The `HttpConnectionManagerImplTest` base class provides all necessary mocks (codec, filters, route config, etc.)\n\n2. **Follow established patterns**: Existing tests in `conn_manager_impl_test.cc` demonstrate the pattern of:\n   - Setting up mocks with `EXPECT_CALL`\n   - Using `Invoke()` lambdas to simulate codec behavior\n   - Verifying stats with assertions on counters\n\n3. **Test isolation**: Each gap should have its own test file or be grouped logically with related tests\n\n4. **Runtime parameters**: Use `TestScopedRuntime` for tests that need to override runtime flags (see existing tests for examples)\n\n5. **Connection state verification**: Use assertions on `filter_callbacks_.connection_` state, drain status, and stream counts\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Risk Levels\n\n| Gap | Risk Level | Root Cause |\n|-----|-----------|-----------|\n| Premature Reset Threshold Logic | HIGH | Complex math with runtime parameters |\n| HTTP/1 Safe Drain | HIGH | Diverges from normal drain path |\n| Zombie Stream Cleanup | HIGH | Complex lifecycle coordination |\n| Upgrade Rejection | MEDIUM | Security-sensitive but single code path |\n| Header Validation Errors | MEDIUM | Multiple error cases not all tested |\n| Path Normalization | MEDIUM | Security-critical normalization logic |\n| Metadata Processing | MEDIUM | Filter chain interaction complexity |\n| Watermark Coordination | MEDIUM | Subtle backpressure logic |\n\nAll identified gaps are in code that executes under error conditions or edge cases, making them particularly easy to miss with standard testing but potentially critical for production stability.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3279,"cache_read_input_tokens":86528,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3279},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"55c71d79-369e-4cfe-8142-025a47e7cb45","uuid":"8c7e5f0c-52e3-44c2-9f8b-fbde0e77eb7a"}
{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01Kh2mzSQFDcujuuWj1QNRvU","type":"tool_result","content":"File created successfully at: /workspace/coverage_analysis.md"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"55c71d79-369e-4cfe-8142-025a47e7cb45","uuid":"e596c333-39f9-4c26-a77d-b14237818990","tool_use_result":{"type":"create","filePath":"/workspace/coverage_analysis.md","content":"# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager\n\n## Summary\n\nThis analysis identifies 8 critical test coverage gaps in Envoy's HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) implementation that could allow subtle bugs to slip through. The gaps primarily involve error handling paths, edge cases in connection state management, and complex interactions between filter chains and stream lifecycle management. The most critical gaps involve premature reset detection, HTTP/1 safe drain logic, and zombie stream cleanup coordination.\n\n---\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: Premature Stream Reset Detection with Runtime Threshold Logic\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~702-749 (method `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()`)\n**Risk**: **HIGH**\n\n**Description**:\n\nThe `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` method contains complex threshold logic that triggers connection draining when streams are reset prematurely. The function:\n\n1. Checks a runtime configuration key `PrematureResetTotalStreamCountKey` (default 500)\n2. Implements a counter-based heuristic: `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < limit`\n3. Has recursion prevention via `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` flag\n4. Increments stats only under specific conditions\n5. Performs early return with different conditions depending on whether `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_` exceeds the limit\n\nCurrently, no tests exercise the full decision tree with various combinations of:\n- Stream reset counts just below/above the threshold\n- Runtime parameter override scenarios\n- Recursion prevention correctness\n- Edge case where exactly `limit/2` streams are reset\n\n**Proposed Test**: `PrematureStreamResetTriggersConnectionDrainAtThreshold`\n- **Setup**: Create 251 requests, 251 with premature resets, runtime limit set to 500\n- **Action**: Trigger drain check\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Verify `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` stat is incremented\n  - Verify connection receives `doConnectionClose()` call\n  - Verify flag prevents recursive drain calls\n  - Verify `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` prevents re-entrance\n\n**Why It Matters**: Premature reset detection is a security/abuse-prevention mechanism. Incorrect threshold calculations could allow attackers to exhaust resources or prevent legitimate connection draining. The complex inequality checks are error-prone.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: HTTP/1 Safe Max Connection Duration with Soft Drain\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~769-787 (method `onConnectionDurationTimeout()`, specifically HTTP1 soft drain path)\n**Risk**: **HIGH**\n\n**Description**:\n\nWhen `config_->http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration()` is true and the codec protocol is HTTP/1, the connection manager takes a \"soft drain\" path instead of a graceful drain sequence:\n\n```cpp\nif (config_->http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration() && codec_->protocol() < Protocol::Http2) {\n  stats_.named_.downstream_cx_http1_soft_drain_.inc();\n  soft_drain_http1_ = true;\n} else {\n  startDrainSequence();\n}\n```\n\nThis sets `soft_drain_http1_` flag but doesn't immediately trigger drain. The flag must be checked elsewhere to actually prevent new requests. No tests verify:\n- That soft drain prevents new requests from being accepted\n- That existing requests are allowed to complete\n- That the stat is correctly incremented\n- Interaction between soft drain and max connection duration\n- What happens when non-HTTP1 protocol reaches max duration (should do full drain sequence)\n\n**Proposed Test**: `HTTP1SafeMaxConnectionDurationSoftDrain`\n- **Setup**: Create HTTP/1.1 connection with `http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration=true`, set connection max duration\n- **Action**: Wait for max duration timeout\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Verify `downstream_cx_http1_soft_drain_` is incremented (not `downstream_cx_max_duration_reached_`)\n  - Verify `soft_drain_http1_` flag is set\n  - Create new request and verify it completes without delay\n  - Verify connection doesn't close until all streams finish\n  - Verify stat names distinguish this from other drain types\n\n**Why It Matters**: HTTP/1 safe drain is a special case designed to prevent race conditions. Testing this specific code path is essential because it diverges from normal drain logic and could leave connections in inconsistent states.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: Zombie Stream Cleanup with Watermark Coordination\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~2137-2179 (methods `onCodecEncodeComplete()` and `onCodecLowLevelReset()`)\n**Risk**: **HIGH**\n\n**Description**:\n\nWhen a stream reaches end-of-stream via `doEndStream()`, it becomes a \"zombie stream\" marked by `state_.is_zombie_stream_ = true`. The zombie stream persists until the codec completes encoding. This coordination involves:\n\n1. Checking `state_.codec_encode_complete_` flag\n2. Calling `shouldSkipDeferredCloseDelay()` to determine if close can be immediate\n3. Possibly triggering `connection_manager_.close_connection_on_zombie_stream_complete_`\n4. Calling `checkForDeferredClose()` after stream destruction\n\nThe gap: No tests verify the complete lifecycle of zombie streams under conditions:\n- With deferred close delay vs. immediate close\n- When multiple zombie streams exist in parallel\n- When connection close is triggered while zombies still exist\n- When watermark callbacks fire on a zombie stream\n- Interaction with `connection_manager_.close_connection_on_zombie_stream_complete_` flag\n\n**Proposed Test**: `ZombieStreamCleanupWithConnectionCloseFlag`\n- **Setup**: Create 3 concurrent streams, enable `close_connection_on_zombie_stream_complete_` flag\n- **Action**: Send response with end_stream on all streams nearly simultaneously\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Verify first stream becomes zombie\n  - Verify second and third streams also become zombies\n  - Verify no `doDeferredStreamDestroy()` until codec encode complete\n  - Verify `checkForDeferredClose()` called with correct `skip_delay` value\n  - Verify connection closes after last zombie cleanup\n  - Verify high watermark events don't crash or corrupt state during cleanup\n\n**Why It Matters**: Zombie streams represent a complex state transition that could cause memory leaks, connection hangs, or protocol violations if not handled correctly. The interaction with the deferred close logic is particularly subtle.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: Connection Upgrade Rejection with Smuggling Prevention\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1546-1563 (method `decodeHeaders()`, upgrade rejection path)\n**Risk**: **MEDIUM**\n\n**Description**:\n\nAfter detecting an upgrade request is rejected by the route, the code enforces a strict policy:\n\n```cpp\nif (create_chain_result.upgradeRejected()) {\n  // Close connection to prevent HTTP smuggling via upgrade payload\n  sendLocalReply(Code::UpgradeRequired, /* ... */);\n  connection_manager_.doConnectionClose(...);\n  return;\n}\n```\n\nThe logic prevents HTTP request smuggling when an Upgrade header is present but the route rejects the upgrade. However, tests don't verify:\n- That connection closes when `upgradeRejected()` is true\n- Various upgrade header combinations (CONNECT, Upgrade: websocket, etc.)\n- That the error response is sent before connection close\n- Behavior when upgrade is rejected for different routes\n- Interaction with other connection close conditions\n\n**Proposed Test**: `UpgradeRejectedByRouteClosesConnection`\n- **Setup**: Configure route that rejects WebSocket upgrades\n- **Action**: Send HTTP/1.1 GET request with Upgrade: websocket and Connection: upgrade headers\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Verify `create_chain_result.upgradeRejected()` is true\n  - Verify `sendLocalReply()` called with `Code::UpgradeRequired`\n  - Verify `doConnectionClose()` called\n  - Verify no further data is processed after upgrade rejection\n  - Try sending pipelined request after upgrade rejection - verify it's rejected\n\n**Why It Matters**: HTTP request smuggling is a critical security vulnerability. This code path protects against a specific smuggling vector, so it must be thoroughly tested to prevent regression.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: Request Header Validation Error Paths\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1415-1432 (method `decodeHeaders()`, header validation section)\n**Risk**: **MEDIUM**\n\n**Description**:\n\nThe `decodeHeaders()` method performs multiple sanity checks on request headers:\n\n1. Line 1415-1420: Verify Host header exists\n2. Line 1423-1431: Validate headers via `HeaderUtility::requestHeadersValid()`\n3. Line 1427-1429: Handle codec error notification conditionally based on `streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage()`\n\nTest gaps:\n- Missing test for requests without Host header (particularly HTTP/1.1 which requires it)\n- No test for invalid header combinations caught by `HeaderUtility::requestHeadersValid()`\n- The conditional codec error path (line 1427) is not tested: when `streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage()` is false, `handleCodecError()` is called, but when it's true, it's skipped\n- No test verifies that `sendLocalReply()` with `Code::BadRequest` is actually sent\n- No tests for header combinations that pass Host check but fail validity check\n\n**Proposed Test**: `InvalidRequestHeadersTriggersLocalReply`\n- **Setup**: Two variants - one with missing Host header, one with invalid header combination\n- **Action**: Send request with missing/invalid headers\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Verify `sendLocalReply(Code::BadRequest, ...)` called\n  - Verify response code details match (MissingHost vs other)\n  - For variant 2: Verify `handleCodecError()` called when `streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage()` is false\n  - Verify stats incremented\n  - Verify stream is terminated after local reply\n\n**Why It Matters**: Header validation is a first-line defense against malformed requests. Incomplete testing could allow invalid requests to progress through the filter chain.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 6: Path Normalization with Redirect and Rejection\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~1460-1487 (method `decodeHeaders()`, path normalization section)\n**Risk**: **MEDIUM**\n\n**Description**:\n\nPath normalization has three possible outcomes with different code paths:\n\n1. `NormalizePathAction::Reject` (line 1467) - close connection\n2. `NormalizePathAction::Redirect` (line 1474) - send 307 with Location header\n3. `NormalizePathAction::Continue` (line 1486) - allow request to continue\n4. Special case: gRPC requests with Redirect (line 1468-1469) - reject instead\n\nTest gaps:\n- No test for path normalization returning `Reject` and verifying connection close\n- Limited tests for `Redirect` case with Location header construction\n- No test for the gRPC special case (reject redirect instead of allowing it)\n- No test with UHV disabled (the normalization code is skipped in UHV mode)\n- Stats tracking for `downstream_rq_failed_path_normalization_` and `downstream_rq_redirected_with_normalized_path_` may not be fully tested\n\n**Proposed Test**: `PathNormalizationRejectClosesConnection`\n- **Setup**: Route with path normalization enabled, request with path requiring rejection\n- **Action**: Send request with path like `//foo` or other normalization-requiring path\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Verify path normalization action is `Reject`\n  - Verify `sendLocalReply(Code::BadRequest)` called\n  - Verify `downstream_rq_failed_path_normalization_` stat incremented\n  - Verify connection close is triggered\n  - Verify gRPC request with redirect returns `BadRequest` not `TemporaryRedirect`\n\n**Why It Matters**: Path normalization is security-critical. Path traversal and normalization bypasses are well-known attack vectors.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 7: Metadata Processing with Filter Chain Iteration\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc`\n**Lines**: ~880-920 (method `decodeMetadata()`) and `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` lines ~1650-1656\n**Risk**: **MEDIUM**\n\n**Description**:\n\nMetadata is processed through the decoder filter chain with special handling for newly-added metadata:\n\n1. Initial metadata is passed through filters via `filter_manager_.decodeMetadata()`\n2. During header decoding, filters can add new metadata via `addDecodedMetadata()`\n3. `processNewlyAddedMetadata()` must be called to iterate newly-added metadata through the chain\n4. Metadata can cause stream errors if there are issues\n\nTest gaps:\n- No test for metadata being added by one filter and properly reaching all subsequent filters\n- No test for the case where metadata processing fails or a filter returns error status\n- No test for concurrent metadata and data events (metadata while data is buffered)\n- No test for metadata with deferred stream (when decode is deferred to next I/O cycle)\n- The deferred metadata path (line 1654) has minimal test coverage\n\n**Proposed Test**: `MetadataProcessingWithFilterChainIteration`\n- **Setup**: Create 2 decoder filters, first filter adds metadata in `decodeHeaders()`\n- **Action**: Send request headers, verify metadata flows through filter chain\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Verify first filter receives original metadata (if any)\n  - Verify second filter receives newly-added metadata from first filter\n  - Verify `processNewlyAddedMetadata()` is called\n  - Verify both filters' `decodeMetadata()` called with correct metadata\n  - Test error case: if `decodeMetadata()` on second filter fails, verify stream is reset\n  - Test deferred case: metadata added when stream decode is deferred\n\n**Why It Matters**: Metadata processing affects request routing, rate limiting, and other policy decisions. Bugs here could cause incorrect policy application or filter chain violations.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 8: Concurrent Stream Watermark Coordination with Connection Close\n\n**File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n**Lines**: ~2113-2121 (methods `onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()` and `onBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark()`)\n**Risk**: **MEDIUM**\n\n**Description**:\n\nWhen connection buffers cross watermarks, callbacks are propagated to all active streams:\n\n```cpp\nvoid onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark() {\n  codec_->onUnderlyingConnectionAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark();\n}\n```\n\nThis calls the codec which propagates to individual streams. Test gaps:\n- No test for watermark callback when connection is draining\n- No test for watermark callback when some streams are zombies\n- No test for what happens if a filter throws exception in watermark callback\n- No test for rapid watermark threshold crossing (above/below/above/below)\n- No test for watermark callback interacting with stream idle timeout\n- Interaction with filter callbacks like `callHighWatermarkCallbacks()`\n\n**Proposed Test**: `WatermarkCallbackDuringConnectionDrain`\n- **Setup**: Create 2 concurrent streams, set write buffer low watermark\n- **Action**:\n  1. Fill write buffer to trigger high watermark\n  2. Start drain sequence\n  3. Continue receiving data to trigger more writes\n  4. Drain write buffer to trigger low watermark\n- **Assertions**:\n  - Verify high watermark callbacks don't crash during drain\n  - Verify low watermark callbacks don't crash during drain\n  - Verify stream codec callbacks coordinated with connection callbacks\n  - Verify filters' high/low watermark callbacks called for each stream\n  - Verify no deadlock with concurrent watermark events\n\n**Why It Matters**: Watermark handling under drain conditions is subtle. Backpressure coordination bugs could cause buffer overflows, deadlocks, or connection leaks.\n\n---\n\n## File References\n\n### Key Implementation Files Analyzed:\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` (2500+ lines, complex state machine)\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h` (header definitions and interfaces)\n- `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` (filter chain execution)\n- `source/common/http/filter_manager.h` (filter manager state)\n\n### Test Files Analyzed:\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc` (main tests)\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_2.cc` (response ordering tests)\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_3.cc` (filter body injection tests)\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_base.h` (test base class with mocks)\n- `test/common/http/conn_manager_misc_test.cc` (miscellaneous tests)\n\n### Supporting Test Infrastructure:\n- `test/mocks/http/mocks.h` (mock codec, encoder, decoder)\n- `test/mocks/router/mocks.h` (mock route config)\n\n---\n\n## Recommendations for Test Implementation\n\n1. **Use existing test infrastructure**: The `HttpConnectionManagerImplTest` base class provides all necessary mocks (codec, filters, route config, etc.)\n\n2. **Follow established patterns**: Existing tests in `conn_manager_impl_test.cc` demonstrate the pattern of:\n   - Setting up mocks with `EXPECT_CALL`\n   - Using `Invoke()` lambdas to simulate codec behavior\n   - Verifying stats with assertions on counters\n\n3. **Test isolation**: Each gap should have its own test file or be grouped logically with related tests\n\n4. **Runtime parameters**: Use `TestScopedRuntime` for tests that need to override runtime flags (see existing tests for examples)\n\n5. **Connection state verification**: Use assertions on `filter_callbacks_.connection_` state, drain status, and stream counts\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Risk Levels\n\n| Gap | Risk Level | Root Cause |\n|-----|-----------|-----------|\n| Premature Reset Threshold Logic | HIGH | Complex math with runtime parameters |\n| HTTP/1 Safe Drain | HIGH | Diverges from normal drain path |\n| Zombie Stream Cleanup | HIGH | Complex lifecycle coordination |\n| Upgrade Rejection | MEDIUM | Security-sensitive but single code path |\n| Header Validation Errors | MEDIUM | Multiple error cases not all tested |\n| Path Normalization | MEDIUM | Security-critical normalization logic |\n| Metadata Processing | MEDIUM | Filter chain interaction complexity |\n| Watermark Coordination | MEDIUM | Subtle backpressure logic |\n\nAll identified gaps are in code that executes under error conditions or edge cases, making them particularly easy to miss with standard testing but potentially critical for production stability.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
